# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Java Dependency Injection with Kafka Plugin Architecture

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the plugin/extension loading system: the PluginClassLoader, the plugin scanning via reflection, and the interface-based dependency injection used for Connector, Converter, and HeaderConverter plugins.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Perfect! I've successfully completed the analysis of Apache Kafka's plugin/extension loading system. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've created a comprehensive answer file (`/workspace/answer.json`) documenting all **32 Java source files** that implement Apache Kafka's plugin/extension loading system, including:

### Key Components:

1. **Class Loading & Isolation** (5 files):
   - `PluginClassLoader` - Custom URLClassLoader for plugin isolation
   - `DelegatingClassLoader` - Parent classloader delegating to multiple PluginClassLoaders
   - `ClassLoaderFactory` - Factory pattern for classloader creation
   - `LoaderSwap` - Try-with-resources helper for classloader switching

2. **Plugin Discovery & Scanning** (5 files):
   - `PluginScanner` - Abstract base for discovery implementations
   - `ReflectionScanner` - Reflection-based scanning using ClassGraph
   - `ServiceLoaderScanner` - Java ServiceLoader mechanism
   - `PluginSource` & `PluginScanResult` - Plugin source and result containers

3. **Plugin Management** (8 files):
   - `Plugins` - Main orchestrator for plugin discovery and instantiation
   - `PluginDesc` - Descriptor for discovered plugins with version tracking
   - `PluginType`, `PluginDiscoveryMode`, `PluginUtils` - Supporting classes

4. **Plugin Interfaces** (7 files):
   - Base interfaces: `Connector`, `SinkConnector`, `SourceConnector`
   - Data format interfaces: `Converter`, `HeaderConverter`
   - Processing interfaces: `Transformation`, `Predicate`
   - Extension interfaces: `ConnectRestExtension`, `ConnectorClientConfigOverridePolicy`

5. **Dependency Injection & Configuration** (7 additional files):
   - `Plugin` wrapper class with metrics integration
   - Configuration management via Configurable interface
   - `ConnectMetrics`, 
... (truncated)

system is implemented in the connect module using a sophisticated architecture that supports interface-based dependency injection for Connector, Converter, and HeaderConverter plugins. Connector: Base interface for all connectors with lifecycle methods (start, stop, taskClass, taskConfigs, config).\\n   - SinkConnector/SourceConnector: Specialized connector interfaces for data sink and source operations.\\n   - Converter: Interface for translating between Kafka Connect's runtime data format and byte arrays, discoverable via ServiceLoader.\\n   - HeaderConverter: Similar to Converter but specifically for header values, with implementation examples like SimpleHeaderConverter.\\n   - ConnectMetrics: Metrics framework for tracking plugin usage (PluginMetrics class wraps plugin instances with automatic metric registration for converters, transformations, predicates).\\n   - WorkerConfig: Centralized configuration with PLUGIN_PATH_CONFIG for specifying isolation directories and PLUGIN_DISCOVERY_CONFIG for choosing discovery strategy.\\n   - TaskPluginsMetadata and TransformationStage: Runtime structures managing plugin instances for task execution, including predicate chaining and conditional transformation.\\n\\nThe system supports multi-versioning through VersionRange specifications, allowing different plugin versions to coexist. Isolation is achieved through separate PluginClassLoaders with child-first delegation, preventing version conflicts between plugins and the framework. Configuration is injected via standard Configurable interface, and plugins are discovered either reflectively (slower but no manifest requirement) or via ServiceLoader (faster but requires manifests). The dependency injection is implicit through interface contracts and explicit through the ConfigDef specification mechanism, enabling flexible plugin composition and configuration validation.\"\n}\n",
